<div id="review_841107850" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/841107850" />
    <a title="Eilonwy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy"><img alt="Eilonwy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506803497p2/17237503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/841107850?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eilonwy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eilonwy" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy">Eilonwy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=character-driven">character-driven</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=deeply-thoughtful">deeply-thoughtful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=really-good-voice">really-good-voice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=heartwarming">heartwarming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=just-brilliant">just-brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=love-story">love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=new-direction-for-this-author">new-direction-for-this-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841107850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4823105161115351635">Four and a half stars. <br/><blockquote>
  <i>Judith disappeared from her home for two years, held captive by a hermit. Then she was allowed to return ... with half her tongue cut out. She is shunned by the townsfolk, and even her mother won't let her speak. She can only think, addressing her thoughts to Lucas, the boy she has loved since she was a baby. But one day the town is attacked. Judith is forced to literally revisit her past, setting off a chain of events which leads to secrets revealed -- and a voice rega</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4823105161115351635" style="display:none">Four and a half stars. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Judith disappeared from her home for two years, held captive by a hermit. Then she was allowed to return ... with half her tongue cut out. She is shunned by the townsfolk, and even her mother won't let her speak. She can only think, addressing her thoughts to Lucas, the boy she has loved since she was a baby. But one day the town is attacked. Judith is forced to literally revisit her past, setting off a chain of events which leads to secrets revealed -- and a voice regained.</i>
</blockquote>I was very curious about this book, as Julie Berry's previous two books were more middle-grade-level high fantasies. This is a huge departure from those, from what I can tell -- much more mature and much darker. <br /> <br />This story carries huge echoes of the Elizabeth Smart abduction in 2002-2003, and I doubt it's coincidence that Julie Berry is also a Mormon. However, the story has been transported from the modern world to Puritan times, with their rigid focus on propriety and feminine "purity." <br /> <br />The first third of this book is absolutely amazing. Judith describes her current life, the time she spent with her abductor, and her witnessing of the murder of a friend in a swirling stream-of-consciousness mix that is eerily beautiful and utterly gripping. I was completely absorbed into this portion of the story -- it's evocative, emotional, and vivid. <br /> <br />The rest of the book then becomes more linear and more of a love story, so that opening punch is lost a bit -- but it remains deeply felt and intense as Judith shows the abrasiveness of her daily life as people feel free to talk in front of her as if she is stupid as well as mute, and their assumptions about her sexual status and perceived availability to men. The abrasiveness is softened by the kindness shown towards Judith by another young woman who wishes to be friends, by Judith's brother, and by Lucas. <br /> <br />I don't want to say too much else for fear of spoilers. <br /> <br />This is a highly unusual, powerful, and heartfelt novel that shows the worst -- and the best -- of human nature. Very strongly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4823105161115351635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_680518888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680518888?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680518888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16474856990744772795">Strange, original, compelling and intense, I found this book, said to YA, very addicting. Second person narrative, shortish comments and thoughts and yet wonderful. The book does actually name a time period,  but it has the tone of The Scarlet Letter, also women called Goody and the stocks for punishment, so this novel is set in the very judgmental Puritan times.<br/><br/>Judith is a wonderful character, a strong young woman with an unquenchable spirit. While reading this I often thought I knew what was g</span>
  <span id="freeText16474856990744772795" style="display:none">Strange, original, compelling and intense, I found this book, said to YA, very addicting. Second person narrative, shortish comments and thoughts and yet wonderful. The book does actually name a time period,  but it has the tone of The Scarlet Letter, also women called Goody and the stocks for punishment, so this novel is set in the very judgmental Puritan times.<br /><br />Judith is a wonderful character, a strong young woman with an unquenchable spirit. While reading this I often thought I knew what was going on, but I was only partly right, there were still surprises to be found. An interesting story, told about a very hypocritical time, a time that did not favor women or for that matter anyone that was different. Judith is different but not because of her own actions but because of what she has suffered.<br /><br />There was a bit of melodrama to the ending, but due to the target audience of this book it was very fitting. All is answered and all is explained. Sometimes having a voice is a very important asset and I loved how this author used hers in writing this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16474856990744772795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_655336960" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655336960" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10951423-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342284001p2/10951423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655336960?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/10951423-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10951423-christine?shelf=sparks-inner-feminist">sparks-inner-feminist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10951423-christine?shelf=ugly-crying">ugly-crying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10951423-christine?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10951423-christine?shelf=i-feel-the-creeps">i-feel-the-creeps</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655336960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17778554464168063723"><b>
  <i>Quick Preview</i>
</b>:<br/>No one knows what happened to Judith and Lottie when they disappeared 4 years ago. Two years afterwards, Judith comes back mutilated and lacking the ability to speak. The people she once knew shun her. Even her own mother won't call her by her real name. She finds herself longing after Lucas, her childhood friend, who have always been the one to understand her. When Roswell Station is attacked, things take a turn, and the truth begins to unravel. Judith struggles with the decis</span>
  <span id="freeText17778554464168063723" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Quick Preview</i>
</b>:<br />No one knows what happened to Judith and Lottie when they disappeared 4 years ago. Two years afterwards, Judith comes back mutilated and lacking the ability to speak. The people she once knew shun her. Even her own mother won't call her by her real name. She finds herself longing after Lucas, her childhood friend, who have always been the one to understand her. When Roswell Station is attacked, things take a turn, and the truth begins to unravel. Judith struggles with the decision whether to stay silent or to find her once lost voice.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Thoughts</i>
</b>:<br />I was a little hesitant to read <i>All the Truth That's in Me</i> at first because it seemed very intense. Having already read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13503247.Flawed" title="Flawed by Kate Avelynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Flawed</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11958608.Uses_for_Boys" title="Uses for Boys by Erica Lorraine Scheidt" rel="nofollow noopener">Uses for Boys</a>, both with dark atmospheres, I wasn't sure if I was ready to plunge into another serious book. I then decided I should just read it, and I'm so glad I did. <br /><br />Let me just say that the cover is perfect. <br />I knew beforehand that this was the type of book that keeps you guessing until the end. At first, I thought that might be somewhat frustrating for me, but it never appeared as a problem when I was reading. The format of the book is written almost like a letter, or as if Judith is telling her friend of an old memory. It was different and written magnificently. This story takes place a while back, in a small town where everyone knew each other and went to church. (Sort of like the setting in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_" title="Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Creatures</a>)<br /><br />During the story, I found myself feeling for Judith, and the tears never stopped coming. Honestly, I felt like I was crying for her and for every bad thing that came along. I don't think I had felt so bad for a character in my entire life. The other characters were well developed. They all played a role in this book, and I didn't feel like there were any unnecessary characters. While reading, I completely despised her mom. She was terrible and insensitive. I don't want to give away too much, but man, she was bad. Judith seemed so alone, so I was grateful for the friendships she made. This was one of those books that have the potential to be life changing.<br /><br />Throughout the book, people treat Judith so cruelly for crimes she never committed, and I couldn't help but hope that Judith gets her happy ending. I won't spoil anything, but I hope you pick up this whirlwind of a book when it comes out on September 26. Seriously, read this book. You want to, trust me. It's amazing.<br /><br />By the way, I'm so honored to be able to read this book before its release date. **I won a copy at I Read to Relax's BEA event giveaway.<br />Thanks to Kendra Levin, and Viking Children's Books for providing ARCs.* My having a copy did not influence the contents of this review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17778554464168063723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757973619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15604542499351703007">I don't normally read historical fiction, but if there are more books as good as this one, I'm sure going to read more of this genre.<br/><br/>This book is hauntingly beautiful, and I love everything about it, even the parts that wrecked my heart.<br/><br/>The story was so captivating that I couldn't think of anything else, but this book - how Judith's life was going be, who had done that to her and why. Just several pages in, I wept like a baby. My heart ached for her and what she had to go through. Being shunned </span>
  <span id="freeText15604542499351703007" style="display:none">I don't normally read historical fiction, but if there are more books as good as this one, I'm sure going to read more of this genre.<br /><br />This book is hauntingly beautiful, and I love everything about it, even the parts that wrecked my heart.<br /><br />The story was so captivating that I couldn't think of anything else, but this book - how Judith's life was going be, who had done that to her and why. Just several pages in, I wept like a baby. My heart ached for her and what she had to go through. Being shunned and discriminated against even when she herself was a victim was just so cruel beyond words could describe.<br /><br />This is one of the books that I will find time to reread. Because once is not enough.<br /><br /><b>(Some) Favorite Quotes</b><br /><br />"You are the sun in my world, and how can I endure to watch you set into another woman's arms?"<br /><br />"If you'd let me, I'd kiss away your fear, and let you rest yourself upon me, and I, I would die beside you and count my self lucky."<br /><br />"If you were mine I'd comfort you; if you were mine you'd need no comfort."<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1056604760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1056604760" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13295112-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410639046p2/13295112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_1712861602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712861602" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712861602?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=instalove-express">instalove-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=baa-baa-black-sheep">baa-baa-black-sheep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=everyone-loves-but-me">everyone-loves-but-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712861602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1493610373990775519"><b>
  <i>”I don’t believe in miracles, but if the need is great, a girl might make her own miracle.<br/><br/>Even if that means enlisting the devil’s help.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I hate it when this happens.<br/><br/><b>I hate it when I don’t like a book that everyone else seems to love.</b> Does anyone else feel that way? It makes me want to personally apologize to it and get into a big spiel about how it’s me and not them. Especially when you scroll through three pages of reviews and come to the slow realization that your rating will probably be t</span>
  <span id="freeText1493610373990775519" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”I don’t believe in miracles, but if the need is great, a girl might make her own miracle.<br /><br />Even if that means enlisting the devil’s help.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I hate it when this happens.<br /><br /><b>I hate it when I don’t like a book that everyone else seems to love.</b> Does anyone else feel that way? It makes me want to personally apologize to it and get into a big spiel about how it’s me and not them. Especially when you scroll through three pages of reviews and come to the slow realization that your rating will probably be the lowest of the bunch.<br /><br />The premise sounded so interesting, and was quite possibly the only good thing about this book. A girl and her friend disappear in the woods and only one of them comes back but unable to speak because her captor cut her tongue out. A social pariah among her town, she pours out her unspoken thoughts and feelings to her childhood friend and unrequited love, Lucas.<blockquote>
  <i>”No one calls me by my name.<br />Young children do not know it.<br />I remind myself each day at sunrise, lest one day I forget.<br />Judith is my name.”</i>
</blockquote>This book couldn’t decide what time period it wanted to be in. This probably doesn’t bug a lot of people, and normally it doesn’t bug me. But there were so many different elements of different time periods that I was completely confused as to when (and more specifically where), this book was set. The prologue gives off the vibe that it’s set in pre-colonial America. The hints of homestead life make it sound like we’re in the 1800s (possibly 1840s-1860s, if I had to take an educated guess). Towards the middle there’s a war going on, making it seem like it’s taking place in the 1700s. A 200 year timespan in which I could make an educated guess on when this takes place doesn’t make it very clear, does it? For a history buff such as myself, mishmashing time periods doesn’t sit well with me when they aren’t explicitly stated. <br /><br />Secondly, the book perpetrates to be one thing, but I got a totally different vibe. I was expecting this to be more of a psychological mystery as to who (or what), took Judith and her friend into the woods. Maybe I was also expecting a tale of vigilante vengeance as Judith seeks justice for her best friend and herself. But that never happened. What I did get was a lot of teenage bemoaning how Lucas doesn’t love her, <b>which you’ll hear about over</b>...<blockquote>
  <i>”You are the sun in my world, and how can I endure to watch you set into another woman’s arms?”</i>
</blockquote><b>And over</b>...<blockquote>
  <i>”All the other little broken hearts- and there are bound to be many- will burn on the altar to your youthful beauty and love. It’s thin comfort to think I’m not alone in my woe.”</i>
</blockquote><b>And over again.</b>...<blockquote>
  <i>”We came here by ship, you and I.<br />I remember my mother telling tales of the trip when I was young. Now she never speaks of it at all.<br />She said I spent the whole trip wide-eyed, watching you.”</i>
</blockquote> It got to the point where it became rather ridiculous. Which leads me to the third and final problem.<br /><br />This book is told in second person POV. Since Judith can’t speak, she’s telling the story, in her head, to Lucas, her childhood friend and crush. It’s like an old-timey version of Lucy and Schroeder from the Peanuts comic strips. Second person POV is extremely tough to pull off in terms of writing, and few books can pull it off well. In some cases, it works. Unfortunately, in this case, <b>it comes off more stalkerish than something groundbreaking</b> or adding something new to the story. What should be a sweet, unrequited love story comes off as a teenage girl completely obsessed, from sneaking out of her own house to watch him leave his house;<blockquote>
  <i>”I watched your cabin as long as I could before I had to hurry back, lest Mother notice me missing.”</i>
</blockquote>to waxing fairly poetic, thinly veiled threats against his intended;<blockquote>
  <i>”Will she? Will her soft hands spin your wool, and bind your wheat into sheaves, and pluck the grubs off your potatoes? Will her china face turn bronze beside you as you labor in your fields?”</i>
</blockquote>; and, finally, going full on Heathcliff from <i>Wuthering Heights</i> on the poor kid by offering to commit suicide and haunt him for the rest of his days.<blockquote>
  <i>”I would leave this errand, follow the horses, and fly to your side. If you’d let me, I’d kiss away your fear, and let you rest yourself upon me, and I, I would die beside you and count myself lucky.”</i>
</blockquote> So romantic, I know.<br /><br />In short, this book has the barest inklings of being a beautiful masterpiece but ends up being a convoluted mess. Warring time periods, failed usage of second person POV, a misleading premise, and a character who is more interested in getting her crush to notice and love her instead of finding justice for herself and her dead best friend make this a disappointing read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1493610373990775519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_694821027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694821027" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694821027?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694821027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8281585883153197904">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>Judith was abducted 2 years ago, and has now returned home with her tongue cut out.<br/>She lives in a small village community, in a non-modern time, and is made to feel pretty worthless.<br/>She fancies a boy called Lucas, but it seems clear to everyone but her, that he will never marry her.<br/>Why was Judith abducted? Why was she returned? What did she suffer during her 2 years of captivity? And what truths is she unable to tell?<br/><br/><br/>This was a really strange book, and not at </span>
  <span id="freeText8281585883153197904" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />Judith was abducted 2 years ago, and has now returned home with her tongue cut out.<br />She lives in a small village community, in a non-modern time, and is made to feel pretty worthless.<br />She fancies a boy called Lucas, but it seems clear to everyone but her, that he will never marry her.<br />Why was Judith abducted? Why was she returned? What did she suffer during her 2 years of captivity? And what truths is she unable to tell?<br /><br /><br />This was a really strange book, and not at all what I was expecting.<br /><br />Judith was an okay character, but living in her head felt a bit messy! As the story went on I began to realise why she was voluntarily mute, but I kinda wished she’d speak up and stand up for herself a bit, and I hated how women were treated as lesser than the men in Judith’s society.<br /><br />This book was not what I was expecting at all. I was expecting a mystery/ suspense story, and instead I got this strange historical fiction/mystery story. I thought that this would be a mystery about Judith’s disappearance, but instead it seemed to be more about her life after she returned, and the way that people behaved towards her.<br /><br />The writing was also odd. In places I appreciated in, and in others I didn’t. At times it was almost like poetry, whilst at others the odd, choppy, stilted sentences were just irritating. It definitely took time for me to get into this book, and I did eventually begin to catch on to the way the author had written the book, but unfortunately for me, by the time I had begun to appreciate the book, the storyline just went downhill, and I was bored.<br /><br />The ending was actually okay, although I was pleased that the book was shorter than I thought. I was pleased that there was a happy ending, but I can’t say that I really enjoyed getting there.<br />This book was just nothing like what I was expecting, and I think a lot of people will find this difficult to appreciate. I had no idea that this book didn’t have a contemporary setting, and I think a lot of people will feel exactly the same way.<br />Overall; a strange historical fiction story, with a very different writing style.<br />4.5 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8281585883153197904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_717420899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717420899" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3701038-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581609995p2/3701038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717420899?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/3701038-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=sromance">sromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3701038-elena?shelf=disability">disability</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717420899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16433365330515968234">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>This book wasn't what I expected, I think because the cover screams contemporary at me (SO MUCH EYELINER). This isn't contemporary. It's a lovely and dark and heartbreaking and triumphant historical novel about a girl named Judith who is back in her suspicious small town after a prolonged absence during which time who-knows-what happened to her--Judith can't say, since she no longer has a tongue. Judith's mother and brother don't treat her terribly well, and she continues to carry a to</span>
  <span id="freeText16433365330515968234" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />This book wasn't what I expected, I think because the cover screams contemporary at me (SO MUCH EYELINER). This isn't contemporary. It's a lovely and dark and heartbreaking and triumphant historical novel about a girl named Judith who is back in her suspicious small town after a prolonged absence during which time who-knows-what happened to her--Judith can't say, since she no longer has a tongue. Judith's mother and brother don't treat her terribly well, and she continues to carry a torch for her neighbor, Lucas, who seemed inclined to return her sentiments until she disappeared. Now he's engaged to the town's Mean Girl, but Judith can't help but cling to her crush since he's the bright spot in her otherwise awful existence.<br /><br />This book was very choppy and the style was unusual, things that are usually big book turnoffs for me, but for some reason this book grabbed me and wouldn't let go. Seriously, I stayed up all night to finish it. This book made me cry, cringe, and cheer. I ached in sympathy for Judith, I rooted for her as she fought to overcome all sorts of challenges (including but not limited to: confronting her past, keeping calm in battle, standing up to her mother, embarking on a new friendship, fighting to educate herself against the odds, being brave enough to speak, being brave enough to speak <i>up</i>, giving the smackdown to pedophiles, going after what she wants out of life), and in the end, I wanted to hug her. <br /><br />This is one of those books you want to snuggle when it's over because your emotions have been yanked around so much that you feel that you and the book have been through an ordeal together. Much love.<br /><br />Updated 5/21/14 to add trigger warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Physical and emotional abuse, extreme sexual harassment, attempted rape <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16433365330515968234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_604990860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604990860" />
    <a title="Tee loves Kyle Jacobson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2566871-tee-loves-kyle-jacobson"><img alt="Tee loves Kyle Jacobson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459255542p2/2566871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604990860?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tee loves Kyle Jacobson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tee loves Kyle Jacobson" href="/user/show/2566871-tee-loves-kyle-jacobson">Tee loves Kyle Jacobson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2566871-tee-loves-kyle-jacobson?shelf=june-2013">june-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2566871-tee-loves-kyle-jacobson?shelf=around-the-world-arc-tours">around-the-world-arc-tours</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604990860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6014157748036223609">Okay first off I am going to say that this book was a weird read for me and for this I gave it a five.I mean the world was set up where it was kinda strict and the people who lived in this town were prudes and they had set ways of doing things and for that I am not going to lie I was like WTF am I reading????????? But then I continued on and the book really started to pick up and held me captive until the very last page where it left me with more questions than answers. So I know I will be readi</span>
  <span id="freeText6014157748036223609" style="display:none">Okay first off I am going to say that this book was a weird read for me and for this I gave it a five.I mean the world was set up where it was kinda strict and the people who lived in this town were prudes and they had set ways of doing things and for that I am not going to lie I was like WTF am I reading????????? But then I continued on and the book really started to pick up and held me captive until the very last page where it left me with more questions than answers. So I know I will be reading this book again when it comes out because I feel like I missed something while I was reading and being all mad at some of the characters I did miss somethings.<br /><br />This is such a strange story about a girl Judith and her best friend who were kidnapped. After two years Judith comes back and is unable to speak because she was tortured and an unspeakable act has been done to her. Being totally mutilated and unable to speak Judith is treated like an outcast and even her teacher who is a filthy disgusting pig does something to her and she can't speak so it goes away like it never happened.<br /><br />But one bright spot in Judith's crazy life is her love for Lucas. She is crushing on him so bad and at first Lucas does not know about her crush but eventually he finds out. Lucas is a great character and what happens after he finds out Judith likes him is the crux of the story and I will not spoil it for anyone but this is a must read because stuff starts popping off!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6014157748036223609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665278300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17664512047939335318"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Hmm, this was an interesting one. It really wasn't what I was expecting, so that was cool. The style of it was unique and engaging––although the super-short chapters and use of second person were sometimes a bit irritating, I thought they still worked most of the time. I found the characters a little lacking and the end felt rushed to me (and maybe not very realistic, either). But over all I thought it was a memorable and intriguing book, and different from anything I've read in a while</span>
  <span id="freeText17664512047939335318" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Hmm, this was an interesting one. It really wasn't what I was expecting, so that was cool. The style of it was unique and engaging––although the super-short chapters and use of second person were sometimes a bit irritating, I thought they still worked most of the time. I found the characters a little lacking and the end felt rushed to me (and maybe not very realistic, either). But over all I thought it was a memorable and intriguing book, and different from anything I've read in a while.<br /><br />Longer review coming eventually!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B2Oxsuhe9lXM5F4WKH9zDtHl7ux2r7T933/3Ijp0UXAFXKkT2ceLTrsV2ymXLiF8bvT/3R+w9r/D7V4xHnjzLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NY0FAq+VY2n8Yjq2ZNZGfwdBxSW34gxrS5MJ7ZcGydI3sh2jngwecouTv4nbhxQNuFDUFN79TilXAaD+swprjA==')})
  }

Polly Longden\'s china-doll looks belie a strong and fiery personality. When typhoid strikes her home city of Lincoln, she needs every ounce of that strength in order to cope. With the death of her mother, thirteen-year-old Polly has to give up her ambition of becoming a teacher to care for her family. When their father, too, falls victim to the typhoid, his only hope is to go to hospital, leaving Polly to cope alone.
